## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt, the time-derivative of population size P(t), which is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth models in ecology. With only (t, P) available, likely relationships include per-capita growth laws, density dependence (crowding/carrying capacity), time-varying environments, and harvesting/mortality terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric/scale-dependent per-capita effects; flexible phenomenology)
- Linear time-varying growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (environmental trend changing intrinsic growth with time)
- Logistic ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density dependence with carrying capacity K = 1/c1)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized density dependence; c2 tunes how sharply limitation kicks in)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic density dependence; asymmetric approach to an upper level)
- Richards (generalized logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (very flexible S-shaped dynamics via additional shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative at low P; bistability with an extinction threshold)
- Allee effect (weak, additive form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P * exp(-c3 * P) (reduced growth at low density without necessarily making it negative)
- Crowding via exponential suppression (Ricker-like continuous): dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (per-capita growth decreases approximately exponentially with density)
- Density-dependent mortality term: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (births proportional to P, deaths from competition proportional to P^2)
- Harvesting/constant removal: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield; can induce collapse at low P)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (exploitation proportional to population size)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)) (periodic environment affecting growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth identification: g(P,t) = dP_dt / P; if g is ~constant → exponential-like growth; if g decreases ~linearly with P → logistic-type density dependence.
- Carrying capacity from zeros: if dP_dt crosses 0 at P≈P* and the slope is negative there, P* is a stable equilibrium (often interpretable as a carrying capacity).
- Allee effect signature: dP_dt < 0 at small P but > 0 at intermediate P implies a critical threshold (unstable equilibrium) separating extinction vs persistence.
- Competition vs self-limitation: a dominant -P**2 term indicates pairwise competition (mass-action encounters), while log(c/P) forms indicate multiplicative/relative limitation (Gompertz).
- Exponential-in-P suppression: factors like exp(-c*P) imply rapidly increasing crowding or contact inhibition at higher densities (Ricker-like behavior).
- Seasonality/forcing: sinusoidal dependence on t (sin/cos) implies periodic resource or climate effects; amplitude parameters control how strongly cycles modulate growth.
- Harvesting/removal: additive negative constants (-c0) suggest constant-yield harvesting; negative terms proportional to P suggest proportional harvesting or background mortality.
- Shape flexibility for S-curves: extra exponents (theta-logistic/Richards) allow earlier vs later slowdown; larger shape exponents typically make the approach to equilibrium sharper.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG23)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 58

GT (fixed):
\[
0.5980\,(1-\tfrac{P}{32.9394})P\;+\;0.5980\,(1-e^{-0.0768278P})P
\]
So GT is a function of **P only** (no \(t\)), and it has the structural form
\[
\underbrace{aP - bP^2}_{\text{polynomial part}} \;+\; \underbrace{aP - aP e^{-kP}}_{\text{exponential part}}
= (2a)P - bP^2 - aP e^{-kP}
\]
with fixed nonzero \(a=0.5980\), \(b=a/32.9394\neq 0\), \(k=0.0768278\neq 0\).
Key signature: **a \(-P^2\) term and a \(-P e^{-kP}\) term, and no other non-polynomial dependence**.

Below, for each candidate, ask: can we choose its constants so the expression becomes exactly \((\alpha)P + (\beta)P^2 + (\gamma)P e^{\delta P}\) with \(\delta<0\) and no extra terms?

---

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4e^{Pc5}\)
Has an extra standalone \(e^{Pc5}\) term (not multiplied by \(P\)). Only removable by \(c4=0\). Then form becomes \(P^2c0 + P(c1e^{Pc2}+c3)\). But GT needs \(P\) times **(constant + exponential)** *and* a separate linear term; that’s fine. However GT’s exponential term is \(-aP e^{-kP}\) plus also a linear \(+2aP\). Candidate can match by setting \(c2=-k\), \(c1=-a\), \(c3=2a\), \(c0=-b\). This seems plausible **if** no other constraints. Yet note GT has no pure \(P e^{+kP}\) growth; we can set negative exponent. So candidate 1 **can match** after setting \(c4=0\).  
But wait: candidate 1 still has only one linear coefficient \(c3\) plus the exponential contribution at \(P=0\) equals \(c1\) (since \(e^0=1\)), so near 0 it contributes \(Pc1\). That’s fine because GT’s exponential part contributes \(-aP\) at small P, and the polynomial part contributes \(+aP\), totaling \(+aP\) from those two, plus another \(+aP\) from the second \(aP\) term → overall \(2aP\). Candidate can reproduce that with \(c3\) adjusted. So **Candidate 1 matches**.

(We still must check others, but one match is enough for final verdict.)

---

### 2. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + P^{c2}c3e^{Pc4} + c5\log(Pc6+1)\)
Has a log term unless \(c5=0\). Then has two exponentials, one multiplied by \(P\), another by \(P^{c2}\). To match GT, we’d need the second exponential term to vanish (set \(c3=0\)) or become polynomial (impossible because of \(e^{Pc4}\) unless \(c3=0\)). With \(c3=0,c5=0\), left with \(Pc0e^{Pc1}\) only, cannot produce the required \(-bP^2\) polynomial term. No match.

### 3. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + Pc2e^{Pc3} + c4\log(Pc5+1)\)
Kill log via \(c4=0\). Then sum of two \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\) terms; cannot produce a pure \(P^2\) term for all \(P\). No match.

### 4. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3e^{Pc4} + Pc5 + c6\log(Pc7+1)\)
Kill log via \(c6=0\), kill \(P^3\) via \(c0=0\). Combine \(P^2\) terms: \(P^2(c1+c2)\). This can supply \(-bP^2\). Linear term \(Pc5\) supplies part of \(2aP\). Exponential term \(Pc3e^{Pc4}\) can supply \(-aP e^{-kP}\) by \(c4=-k, c3=-a\). Then choose \(c5=2a\). Works. Candidate 4 matches.

### 5. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3 + P^{c4}c5e^{Pc6} + c7\)
Needs no constant term: set \(c7=0\). The \(P^{c2}c3\) term must be either linear/quadratic or vanish; but any non-integer power breaks equality for all \(P\). Could set \(c3=0\). The \(P^{c4}c5e^{Pc6}\) term: to match \(P e^{-kP}\) we’d need \(c4=1\), \(c6=-k\), \(c5=-a\). Then we still need linear \(+2aP\): provided by \(Pc1\) with \(c1=2a\). Quadratic \(-bP^2\): \(c0=-b\). Works with \(c3=0\). Candidate 5 matches.

### 6. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + P^{c4}c5 + c6\)
Set \(c6=0\). The \(P^{c4}c5\) term must vanish or become linear/quadratic; but we already have those. Best set \(c5=0\). Then match as in candidate 1 style: choose \(c0=-b\), \(c1=2a\), \(c2=-a\), \(c3=-k\). Works. Candidate 6 matches.

### 7. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4e^{Pc5}\)
Two \(P e^{(\cdot)P}\) terms; GT needs only one. Set one to zero: e.g. \(c4=0\). Then same as candidate 1 without extra term: choose \(c0=-b\), \(c2=-k\), \(c1=-a\), \(c3=2a\). Matches.

### 8. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + Pc4e^{Pc5} + Pc6 + Pc7\)
Set \(c0=0\). Combine \(P^2\) coefficients to \(-b\). Combine linear terms \(Pc6+Pc7\) to \(2aP\). Exponential term \(Pc4e^{Pc5}\) to \(-aP e^{-kP}\). Works. Matches.

### 9. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3e^{Pc4} + Pc5\)
Set \(c0=0\). Combine \(P^2\) to \(-b\). Set \(c3=-a,c4=-k\). Set \(c5=2a\). Matches.

### 10. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5\)
Need \(P^{c4}c5\) not to introduce non-polynomial. Set \(c5=0\) (or make it linear and absorb, but easiest 0). Then same as candidate 1 core; matches.

### 11. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} + Pc6 + Pc7\)
The \(Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} = c3 c4^{c5} P^{c5+1}\). To avoid extra powers, set \(c3=0\) (or force \(c5=0\) giving another linear term). Either way can reduce to \(P^2\) + linear + \(P e^{\cdot P}\). Choose parameters to match. Matches.

### 12. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\log(Pc5+1)\)
Log must vanish: \(c4=0\). Then matches as candidate 1 core. Matches.

### 13. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + Pc2(1-(Pc3)^{c4})^{c5} + c6\log(Pc7+1)\)
Kill log: \(c6=0\). The middle term is not polynomial/exponential in the needed way for all \(P\) unless set \(c2=0\). Then only \(Pc0e^{Pc1}\), cannot create \(-bP^2\). No match.

### 14. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + \frac{Pc4}{Pc5+c6} + \frac{c7}{Pc5+c6}\)
Rational terms must vanish: set \(c4=0,c7=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 15. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + \frac{Pc3}{P+c4} + Pc5\)
The rational \(\frac{P}{P+c4}\) cannot be identically polynomial/exponential unless \(c3=0\). Then matches core with \(Pc5\) as linear. Matches.

### 16. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + Pc4\)
Combine \(P^2\) to \(-b\). Set exponential to \(-aP e^{-kP}\). Set \(Pc4\) to \(2aP\). Matches.

### 17. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4\)
Combine linear \(Pc3+Pc4\) to \(2aP\). Set \(P^2c0=-bP^2\). Set exponential term to \(-aP e^{-kP}\). Matches.

### 18. \(Pc0(1-(Pc1)^{c2})^{c3} + Pc4e^{Pc5}\)
Hard to get a quadratic term \(-bP^2\) from these forms for all \(P\). The first term is \(P\) times a non-polynomial in general; making it polynomial would require special exponents but still won’t yield an exact linear+quadratic simultaneously without extra higher-order terms. No match.

### 19. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3\)
Exactly the needed structure (quadratic + linear + \(P e^{\cdot P}\)). Choose \(c0=-b\), \(c1=-a\), \(c2=-k\), \(c3=2a\). Matches.

### 20. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + Pc4 + Pc5\)
Same as 16/17 with extra linear; combine. Matches.

### 21. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3e^{Pc4} + Pc5 + Pc6\)
Same; matches.

### 22. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4(1-(Pc5)^{c6})^{c7}\)
Last term generally non-polynomial; set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 23. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + Pc5\)
No \(P^2\) term unless \(c4=1\) gives \(P^2\) but then still lacks the needed \(P e^{-kP}\) *and* linear simultaneously (only one exponential term and remaining are polynomial). Actually first term is \(P e^{Pc1}\) can be the exponential piece, second can be \(P^{c4+1}\) to be quadratic with \(c4=1\). Then linear \(Pc5\) supplies \(2aP\). Works: set \(c1=-k\), \(c0=-a\), \(c4=1\), \(c2c3=-b\), \(c5=2a\). Matches.

### 24. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + c4\)
Need no constant: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 25. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3e^{Pc4} + Pc5 + c6\)
Set \(c6=0\). Combine linear terms \(Pc2+Pc5\). Combine quadratic. Set exponential. Matches.

### 26. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4 + c5\)
Set constant \(c5=0\). Combine linear. Matches.

### 27. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4\log(1+c5/P)\)
Log term depends on \(1/P\); cannot equal GT for all \(P\) unless \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 28. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + P^{c2}c3 + c4\log(Pc5+1)\)
Kill log: \(c4=0\). Need quadratic and linear and exponential. Only one exponential term and one power term. If \(c2=2\) gives quadratic, but then no independent linear term (unless exponential term somehow provides linear too, but it’s \(P e^{Pc1}\) not linear for all \(P\) unless \(c1=0\), which would remove the needed \(e^{-kP}\)). No match.

### 29. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3e^{Pc4} + Pc5 + c6\log(Pc7+1)\)
Kill log: \(c6=0\). Two exponentials; set one to zero (e.g. \(c3=0\)). Then matches core. Matches.

### 30. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\sin(c5\log(c6e^{Pc7}+1)+c8)\)
Sine term must vanish: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 31. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + Pc2e^{Pc3} + Pc4 t e^{Pc5} + c6\log(Pc7+1)\)
Has explicit \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Kill log with \(c6=0\). Then only exponentials, no \(P^2\). No match.

### 32. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4(c5+t)^{c6}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence must set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 33. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4 + Pc5 t\)
Remove \(t\): \(c5=0\). Then matches core (with extra linear). Matches.

### 34. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4 t + c5\)
Remove \(t\): \(c4=0\). Remove constant: \(c5=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 35. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + \frac{c4 t}{Pc5+c6} + \frac{c7}{Pc5+c6}\)
Remove \(t\): \(c4=0\). Remove rational: \(c7=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 36. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4 t (P+c5)^{c6}\)
Remove \(t\): \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 37. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4 t^{c5}\)
Remove \(t\): \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 38. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\log(c5e^{c6 t} + c7(Pc8)^{c9} + 1)\)
Log term must vanish: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 39. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\log(c5 t + 1)\)
Remove \(t\)/log: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 40. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + c4e^{c5 t}\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 41. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4e^{Pc5}\log(c6 t + 1)\)
To remove \(t\), need \(\log(c6 t+1)\) gone: set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 42. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + \frac{c4 t}{c5 t + c6} + \frac{c7}{c5 t + c6}\)
Remove \(t\)-dependence: easiest set \(c4=0,c7=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 43. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\log(c5e^{Pc6 + c7 t} + 1)\)
Log term must vanish: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 44. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + \frac{Pc4}{c5 t + c6} + \frac{c7}{c5 t + c6}\)
To remove \(t\): either make denominator constant by \(c5=0\), then terms become \((c4/c6)P + (c7/c6)\). Need no constant so \(c7=0\). Then it’s just extra linear, OK. Matches (with \(c5=0,c7=0\)).

### 45. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\log(c3e^{Pc4}+1) + c5e^{c6 t}\)
Remove \(t\): \(c5=0\). Log term \(\log(c3e^{Pc4}+1)\) cannot become \(P e^{-kP}\) or polynomial for all \(P\) unless \(c2=0\). Then no exponential term remains. No match.

### 46. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2e^{Pc3} + c4e^{c5 t} + c6\)
Remove \(t\): \(c4=0\). Remove constant: \(c6=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 47. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5e^{c6 t}\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c5=0\) (or \(c6=0\) makes it \(P^{c4}c5\) which is problematic unless tuned). With \(c5=0\), matches core. Matches.

### 48. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\sin(Pc5+c6)\)
Sine must vanish: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 49. (has multiple \(\sin(c2 t+c3)\), exp, log)
To remove \(t\): set coefficients of all \(t\)-dependent sine terms to 0 (those multiplying \(P^2\) and \(P\)), i.e. set the sine amplitudes to 0. Also remove log via its coefficient 0. Then reduces to polynomial + \(P e^{\cdot P}\) + linear, which can match. Matches.

### 50. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5e^{Pc6}\cos(c7 t)\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c5=0\) (or \(c7=0\) makes cos constant 1, but then extra \(P^{c4}e^{Pc6}\) term remains). With \(c5=0\), matches core. Matches.

### 51. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\sin(c5+c6 t)\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 52. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5\sin(c6 t+c7)\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c5=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 53. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4\log(c5e^{c6\sin(Pc7+c8 t+c9)}+1)\)
Log term must vanish: \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 54. (quadratic + sine(t) terms + exp + linear)
Remove \(t\): set sine amplitudes to 0. Then reduces to \(P^2\) + \(P e^{\cdot P}\) + linear, matchable. Matches.

### 55. Similar to 54 without log
Same: zero out sine amplitudes. Matches.

### 56. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + Pc4\sin(c5 t+c6)\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 57. \(P^2c0 + Pc1e^{Pc2} + Pc3 + c4e^{c5\sin(Pc6+c7 t+c8)}\)
To remove \(t\), easiest set \(c4=0\). Then matches core. Matches.

### 58. \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + \frac{Pc2}{Pc3+c4} + c5\log(Pc6+1) + \frac{c7}{Pc3+c4}\)
Kill log: \(c5=0\). Rational terms: \(\frac{Pc2}{Pc3+c4}\) is linear if denominator constant; but it depends on \(P\) unless \(c3=0\). With \(c3=0\), it becomes \((c2/c4)P\) and \((c7/c4)\) constant; need constant 0 so \(c7=0\). Then expression is \(Pc0e^{Pc1} + (\text{linear})\). No \(P^2\) term. No match.
